  102. I really liked these sponges. The blue one's neck is a little thin and flimsy but they all have lasted through many uses. I really liked the seller's follow up information on different ways to clean the sponges. I used the olive oil method. I put a 1/2 teaspoon of extra virgin olive oil in a plastic baggie, then put my sponge inside the bag and worked the oil into the makeup area on the sponge with my hands outside the bag. Then squeezed the makeup/oil out of the sponge while still in the bag and then took it out and cleaned it with a mild soap and air dried it. Voila! No mess on my hands! No makeup stains on my sponge!

I've been using the same sponge for 3 months and I'm just now seeing that I need to replace it. I wash it carefully after each use and set it out overnight to dry. I recommend using a mild cleanser (such as face wash, body wash, or bar soap) that doesn't sud very much to wash it. Once you see the tiny pores of the sponge starting to stretch or tear, it's time to get a new sponge. This will NOT work well with a thick, wax based concealer, and it tends to soak up watery, serum-like foundations, so check ingredients and consistency before purchasing these!<br /><br />Here is how I use the sponge: I saturate the sponge completely in warm water, squeeze out the excess, and blot it with a towel. I first dot liquid foundation all over my face and spread it with my Real Tecniques buffing brush to allow it to oxidize on the skin. I then use the bigger side to &#34;bump&#34; and blend it into my skin, around my hairline, and down my neck. I apply cream concealer under my eyes and problem areas and use the smaller side to blend concealer. The point really helps you get close to your eyes. I then dip the smaller side into translucent powder to set the undereye concealer, then dip in the larger side and pat the powder lightly over my T-zone.<br /><br />I've never used the Beauty Blender, so I can't tell you if it's a dupe, but it does pretty much the same thing.   582. Beauty Blender sponges are a very expensive and specific product. As the sponges wear out,it is logical that you might want to replace your Beauty Blender with another sponge that might cost less and save money over time. Because this purchase is a big decision for many who are considering using it, let's take an in-depth look at how and why these sponges are different, and if they are a choice that you might want to make for your makeup arsenal.<br /><br />Since this is advertised as a Beauty Blender Dupe, I wanted to do this review based upon my uses of both sponges with the same product, applied to the same skin on a few people. I am a makeup artist. I am used to using throw away cosmetic sponges, and I also use the Beauty Blender. When I want an airbrushed finish that uses as little makeup as possible (HD makeup gets expensive) I prefer the Beauty Blender. Let's take a look at why I feel that way.<br /><br />WHAT IS THE DIFFERENCE IN THE TEXTURE AND BEHAVIOR?<br />First of all, the texture of these sponges are different than the beauty blender. The surface texture of these sponges is like flocked fleece. The texture of the Beauty Blender is that of a micro sponge. The surface is uneven and similar to a natural sponge, but much tinier.<br /><br />Secondly the weight of these sponges is more dense and heavier than the Beauty Blender. This reflects also in their ability to absorb water and grow in size. These only get slightly bigger, compared to the Beauty Blender which almost doubles in size.<br /><br />Lastly, the way that these sponges act when using is different. These sponges are more of a stable solid surface which is more of an applicator in nature. The Beauty Blender is much more bouncy and this is important for what I need it for, which I will address next in this review.<br /><br />WHAT KIND OF MAKEUP DO I USE A SPONGE FOR?<br />I like to use makeup that is HD ready so that I know it will photograph well, appear true to color in various light, and also be complimentary on skin of all ages. My goal is to use as little as possible of the foundation, but make the application look like it is actual skin on men or women that I apply it on. Graftobian HD creme is one of my favorites, but I also use MAC Studio Tech on occasions. I like to use the sponge for a flawless application of these foundations in particular, which is why I like using a sponge.<br /><br />I also like to apply corrector and concealer under the eye area using the point, in a way that is not detectable through the day by settling in the lines.<br /><br />HOW DOES THIS SPONGE SET PERFORM AS COMPARED TO BEAUTY BLENDER?<br />The primary reason that I do not like this sponge set for doing foundation is that it is more of a solid stable surface. That means that water is locked into the sponge and when you press it onto the skin surface, it bounces a little, but it does not release much moisture and it also does not redistribute the foundation in a manner which causes it to blend with the skin surface as well as the Beauty Blender.<br /><br />Another thing that I noticed is that these sponges take up a lot more makeup than the Beauty Blender. I can do an entire face barely touching the Beauty Blender to my pan of foundation only a few times. I have used it to cover up very dark bruising, discoloration, and marks on the face so well that no one had any idea that foundation had been used. I also have used the Beauty Blender for corrector and concealer (again cream). The Beauty Blender scored once again with using a lot less product than these sponges use.<br /><br />With these sponges, I found that it was harder to get the foundation, corrector, or concealer to go onto the sponge at first and then too much would get onto the sponge afterward. I only got about a fourth of the mileage out of the application, and most of the foundation still remained on the sponge, but would not distribute to the skin.<br /><br />The biggest problem I had with these sponges was in their retention of moisture without dispersing it with the foundation when applying to the skin. That left the foundation patchy in places and a little bit of streaking despite me using the same bouncing technique that I use with the Beauty Blender.<br /><br />When using the Beauty Blender, the surface of the sponge is soft to the touch, but uneven like a natural sponge is. That allows the sponge to pick up a little foundation with very little effort, and it redistributes the foundation around the skin in such a way that it actually does look like skin when you are done because it incorporates tiny bits of the moisture in the sponge into the application process. It is that moisture mix which leaves the foundation I use looking like a second skin. Without it, it is not nearly as flattering.<br /><br />Dry time is vastly different as well. These sponges take several days to dry completely (you don't want to store them out of airflow until they are dry lest they mold), and my Beauty Blender takes about a day to dry well.<br /><br />ARE THESE SPONGES GOOD FOR ANYTHING ELSE?<br />When using these sponges for cream blush or a couple of cream eye shadow colors, I did find the surface and texture to be better utilized. Since only a small area is being done and the color can be more intense, it did work better for those small things. However, I still prefer the Beauty Blender in the long run, but these would serve as a decent pinch hit in my kit if I needed them for those things.<br /><br />I also think that these sponges would be good to fix up spots quickly that need to be blended or thinned out and not necessarily sponged on with the stippling appearance of the Beauty Blender.<br /><br />CLEANING<br />I will say that the cleaning instructions on these sponges are worth the price of the package. Using the olive oil/soap combo on the sponges also works on the Beauty Blenders. I am amazed at how beautifully the combination cleans the sponges. Kudos to the company for providing such valuable information!<br /><br />THE BOTTOM LINE<br />I have rated this two stars because I don't HATE these sponges, but I wanted them specifically for foundation applications to replace the Beauty Blender, and in that case, these just didn't do it for me with the type of foundation that I like to use. For blush or eye shadow, they were acceptable and will serve me well as a back up in my kit. The texture and performance is quite different than using a Beauty Blender, so if you really want a Beauty Blender, you might not be satisfied with this. It does use a lot more product which is another drawback for me as I want to extend my makeup as much as I can. The price is good and these sponges can be used to clean up spots or for some things well enough, but if you want cream foundation to be applied flawlessly using as little product as possible, I don't think this is the best choice.<br /><br />If you are comfortable using the white throw away sponges that makeup artists use regularly, then this set would be a good choice to consider. They clean up very well if used as instructed, so should provide a decent period of use for you.th these sponges was in their retention of moisture without dispersing it with the foundation when applying to the skin.
